                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Marinated olives, Spanish recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#olives #marinatedolives #sherryvinegar #marinate #greenolives #spices #chillipowder #blackolives #cuminseeds #garlic #olive \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Having realised that I was bored with pre-prepared stuffed olives, I decided to buy plain olives, complete with stones and marinate them\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1950\n|PortionCalories = 65\n|DatePublished=20th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Servings: 30 - Marinades 1.5 kg of olives\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 1 week\n |PrepTime = 1 week\n |CookTime = None\n |Image = [[Image:Olives in marinade.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Never thought of doing this</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Trouble is, can't find raw olives in bulk \ud83d\ude10</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n \n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nHaving realised that I was bored with pre-prepared stuffed [[Olives|olives]], I decided to buy plain olives, complete with stones and [[Marinate|marinate]] them.  I happened to have a lot of olives when I made this, but you easily reduce the quantity.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500 g [[Green olives|green olives]], stones intact\n| 1 kg [[Black olives|black olives]], stones intact\n| [[Olive oil]], to cover\n| 1 bulb or more of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 1-2 teaspoons [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Dried thyme|dried thyme]] or [[Oregano|oregano]]\n| 90 ml [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the olives in an airtight container, such as a [[Lock&Lock boxes|Lock&Lock box]] and add enough olive oil to cover.\n| Stir in the remaining ingredients and shake vigorously.\n| Leave to [[Marinate|marinate]] for at least a week before consumption.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nUse with any recipe that calls for [[Olives|olives]], removing the stones if necessary.  Personally, I just enjoy pigging out on them on their own. \n===Variations===\nTry experimenting with your own choice of [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Spices|spices]].  My green hojiblanca [[Olives|olives]] originated in the area around Fuente de Piedra in Andaluc\u00eda and the black ones were from Syria.  Use any combination of [[Olive|olive]] type, colour and origin.  Make your blend unique!\n===Chef's notes===\nIt is a good idea to shake the container several times daily as the [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]] sinks to the bottom.\n\nRemove the stones if you wish, but I find that [[Olives|olives]] taste better stoned at the last minute.\n\nDo not throw away the [[Marinade|marinade]] as it can be used as a dressing.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#olives #marinatedolives #sherryvinegar #marinate #greenolives #spices #chillipowder #blackolives #cuminseeds #garlic #olive </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

you can use tuna here\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1507\n|PortionCalories = 376\n|DatePublished=19th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Marmitako recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n======Best recipe review======\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Back to Bilbao!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This reminds me of our surfing holidays in the 90's at Biarritz</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> - [[User:Chef|Jerry]]</span></span>\n}}\nA typical Basque recipe based on [[bonito]] (see 'Chef\u2019s notes' below), [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and [[Peppers|peppers]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 250 g [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped\n| [[Garlic]], [[Diced|diced]], to taste\n| 250 g [[Green peppers|green peppers]], finely chopped\n| 1 kg [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and cut into chunks\n| Water or [[Fish stock|fish stock]]\n| 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| [[Salt]] to taste\n| 250 g [[bonito]], [[Diced|diced]]\n| 2 [[Tomatoes]], [[Diced|diced]] (optional)\n| [[Parsley]], chopped, to garnish\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat some [[Olive oil|olive oil]] in a [[Deep frying|deep frying]] pan and gently saut\u00e9 the [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Green peppers|green peppers]] and [[Potatoes|potatoes]] until the [[Onions|onions]] are soft.\n| Cover with sufficient water or [[Fish stock|fish stock]].\n| Add the [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]] and the [[Salt|salt]] and [[Boil|boil]] for about 10 minutes.  Top up with more water if necessary.\n| Add the [[bonito]] and [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] if using, and let it [[Simmer|simmer]] for a further 10 minutes\n| Sprinkle with chopped [[Parsley|parsley]] and serve.\n}}\n===Variations===\nYou can include other small [[Vegetables|vegetables]] such as [[Peas|peas]] and use [[White wine|white wine]] instead of some of the water or [[Stock|stock]].\n===Chef's notes===\n[[Bonito]] is a [[Fish|fish]], which is a cross between [[Mackerel|mackerel]] and [[Tuna|tuna]].  The true bonito (which is darkish) is not easily found in the UK so use [[Tuna steaks|tuna steaks]] instead.  The fish sold in tins called \"Bonito del Norte\", whilst excellent is, in fact, white tuna.\n\nMarmitako tastes better when prepared a day in advance.\n==See also==\n* [[Marmitako]]\n* [[Marmitako (2)]]\n* [[Marmitako (Basque fish stew) (TM)]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Marmitako]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes|Marmitako]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Marmitako]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes|Marmitako]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Marmitako]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Marmitako]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#marmitako #bonito #potatoes #diced #bayleaves #tomatoes #greenpeppers #onion #oliveoil #fishstock #parsley </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

covered, for a further 5 minutes and season to taste.\n| Serve in shallow [[Soup|soup]] plates.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Country bread|country bread]].\n===Chef's notes===\nDo not let the [[Fish|fish]] cook for more than 6 minutes or it will become tough.\n==See also==\n* [[Marmitako]]\n* [[Marmitako (2)]]\n* [[Marmitako (Basque fish stew) [[Sofrito|sofrito]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 50g [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]]\n| 100g [[Green peppers|green peppers]]\n| 150g [[Onions|onions]]\n| 100g tinned Varoma / Reverse Blade / Speed Spoon'''.\n| When the machine stops, incorporate the chopped [[Parsley|parsley]].\n| Adjust seasoning and leave for a few minutes without removing the bowl from the machine.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Country bread|country bread]]. \n===Recipe source===\n* This is a translation of a recipe in '''''[[Thermomix]] TM31 - Imprescindible para tu cocina''''' which is the book supplied with [[Spanish]] TMXs\n===Chef's notes===\nThe final cooking time depends on the type of [[Potatoes|potatoes]] used\n==See also==\n* [[Marmitako]]\n* [[Marmitako (2)]]\n* [[Marmitako (Basque fish stew) (TM)]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#thermomix #potatoes #tuna #parsley #sofrito #paprika #marmitako #bonito #fishstock #tomatoes #spanish </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Mayonesa (TM)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Mayonesa - A Thermomix recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#thermomix #mayonnaise #sunfloweroil #spanish #lemon #cream #yolks #curdled #garlicmayonnaiserecipes #juice #vinegar \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A Spanish Thermomix recipe for mayonnaise\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2855\n|PortionCalories = 68\n|DatePublished=21st September 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = The new [[Thermomix]] TM5 (2014)\n|Servings = Servings: 42 - Makes 850g\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 5 minutes \n|PrepTime = 5 minutes \n|CookTime = None \n|Image = [[Image:The new (2014) Thermomix TM5.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Mayo in my Thermie</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">What could be nicer?</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\nA [[Spanish]] [[Thermomix]] recipe for [[Mayonnaise|mayonnaise]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n| 300g [[Olive|olive]] or [[Sunflower oil|sunflower oil]]\n| 1 [[Egg|egg]], or 2 [[Yolks|yolks]]\n| The [[Juice|juice]] of &frac12; a [[Lemon|lemon]] or 1 tablespoon [[Vinegar|vinegar]]\n| 25g water\n| [[Salt]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Weigh the [[Oil|oil]] by putting a jug on the lid of the [[Thermomix]], press the scales button and pour in the oil until the display shows 300.\n| Put all the ingredients in the bowl, except the [[Oil|oil]], and mix '''10 seconds / Speed 4'''.\n| With the '''MC''' on the lid, program '''Speed 4''' and pour the [[Oil|oil]] onto the lid, little by little.\n| If the [[Mayonnaise|mayonnaise]] curdles, take it out of the bowl and without washing it add 50g hot water and at '''Speed 5''', incorporate the [[Curdled|curdled]] mixture, little by little.\n}}\n===Variations===\nIf you wish, you can use 150g [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and 150g [[Sunflower oil|sunflower oil]].  You can lighten the [[Mayonnaise|mayonnaise]] by adding 100g [[Yoghurt|yogurt]], [[Milk|milk]] or [[Cream|cream]].\n===Recipe source===\n* This is a translation of a recipe in '''''[[Thermomix]] TM31 - Imprescindible para tu cocina''''' which is the book supplied with [[Spanish]] TMXs.\n==See also==\n* A huge variety of [[Garlic mayonnaise recipes|different mayonnaise recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#thermomix #mayonnaise #sunfloweroil #spanish #lemon #cream #yolks #curdled #garlicmayonnaiserecipes #juice #vinegar </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Mayonesa de Leche y Cebolla (Milk and Onion Mayonnaise) (TM)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Mayonesa de Leche y Cebolla Thermomix Onion Mayonnaise recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#onion #vinegar #thermomix #mayonnaise #rice #griddled #lemonjuice #lemon #seafood #boiledpotatoes #fish \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This Milk and Onion Mayonnaise recipe is a translation of a recipe in Salsas y Alinos con Thermomix (Susaeta Ediciones)\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3308\n|PortionCalories = 165\n|DatePublished=13th November 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = The new [[Thermomix]] TM5 (2014)\n|Servings = Servings: 20 - Makes 600 ml\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 8 minutes\n|PrepTime = 5 minutes\n|CookTime = 3 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:The new (2014) Thermomix TM5.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Another Thermy mayo</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.91</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">You can never have too many mayonnaise recipes.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is a translation of a recipe in '''Salsas y Ali\u00f1os con [[Thermomix]] (Susaeta Ediciones)'''\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 200g [[Milk|milk]]\n| 400g [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| A few drops of [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 25g [[Onion|onion]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Vinegar|vinegar]]\n| [[White pepper]]\n| [[Salt]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Peel and cut the [[Onion|onion]], tip it into the TM and chop '''5 seconds / Speed 5'''.\n| Reserve and wash the TM.\n| Put the [[Milk|milk]] in the TM and heat for '''3 minutes / 37\u00b0 / Speed 4'''.\n| Next, add the chopped [[Onion|onion]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]].\n| Beat '''37\u00b0 / Speed 5'''.\n| Without stopping the machine, add the [[Oil|oil]] to the lid, little by little.\n| When the [[Mayonnaise|mayonnaise]] has thickened a little, add the [[Vinegar|vinegar]] and [[Lemon|lemon]].\n| You use roughly double the amount of [[Oil|oil]] to [[Milk|milk]], but if you want a paler colour, you will have to reduce the amount of oil.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThis is a variation of traditional [[Mayonnaise|mayonnaise]].  It can be used to accompany many dishes:  [[Boiled potatoes|boiled potatoes]], [[Steamed|steamed]] [[Vegetables|vegetables]], [[Griddled|griddled]] or steamed [[Fish|fish]], griddled [[Seafood|seafood]] and [[Rice|rice]] and [[Pasta salads|pasta salads]].\n==See also==\n* A huge variety of [[Garlic mayonnaise recipes|different mayonnaise recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onion #vinegar #thermomix #mayonnaise #rice #griddled #lemonjuice #lemon #seafood #boiledpotatoes #fish </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This is a Spanish version\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1463\n|PortionCalories = 243\n|DatePublished=20th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = The new [[Thermomix]] TM5 (2014) \n|Servings = Serves 6 - Makes about 1 litre\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 45 minutes \n|PrepTime = 10 minutes\n|CookTime = 35 minutes \n|Image = [[Image:The new (2014) Thermomix TM5.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice Thermy recipe Julia</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Especially as you're a vegetarian!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nMaking your own [[Stock|stock]] concentrate or cubes is very economical and keeps well without the addition of un-natural chemicals.  This is a [[Spanish]] version\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n| 300g lean [[Meat|meat]], cut into pieces ([[Chicken|chicken]], [[Beef|beef]], [[Pork|pork]])\n| 1 whole [[Tomato|tomato]]\n| 300g various [[Vegetables|vegetables]] ([[Celery|celery]], [[Carrot|carrot]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Leek|leek]], [[Garlic|garlic]] etc.)\n| 30g [[Red wine|red wine]]\n| 1 [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]\n| 1 [[Clove bud]] (optional)\n| 300g [[Coarse salt|coarse salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Meat|meat]] in the bowl to chop it '''10 seconds / Speed 8'''.\n| Remove the [[Meat|meat]] and reserve it.\n| Next, tip in the [[Tomato|tomato]] and all of the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and chop '''10 seconds / Speed 6'''.\n| Incorporate the [[Meat|meat]], [[Wine|wine]], [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]], [[Clove|clove]] and [[Salt|salt]] '''30 minutes / 100\u00b0 / Speed 1'''.\n| If, due to the type of [[Salt|salt]], [[Meat|meat]], etc. that you use, you see a little liquid, program '''5 minutes / Temp. Varoma / Speed 1'''.\n| Leave it to cool in the bowl for a few minutes, then [[Blend|blend]] '''1 minute / Speed 6''' and finally '''1 minute / Speed 10'''.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n* This is a translation of a recipe in '''''[[Thermomix]] TM31 - Imprescindible para tu cocina''''' which is the book supplied with [[Spanish]] TMXs.\n===Chef's notes===\nKeep in a container in the [[Fridge|fridge]].  [[Salt]] is a natural [[Preservative|preservative]].  When the mixture is cold, you can shape it into a 4cm cylinder, cut it into medallions of 2cm thick and wrap them individually in [[Cling film|cling film]] or [[Tin foil|tin foil]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#bayleaf #vegetables #thermomix #spanish #tomato #leek #preservative #garlic #fridge #wine #thermomixrecipes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                "revisions": [

                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Menorcan garlic prawns seafood recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#garlic #brownbread #menorcangarlicprawns #parsley #bread #prawns #tapa #chillies #panfried #gambasalajillo #wedges \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=While on holiday in Menorca recently, this tapa was eaten on a daily basis. It's easy to make at home too!\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 398\n|PortionCalories = 199\n|DatePublished=4th October 2014\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  25 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Menorcan garlic prawns recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Easier than you think</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">You really can make this at home.  It's fabulous, lovely garlic!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nWhile on holiday in Menorca recently, this [[Tapa|tapa]] was eaten on a daily basis!  \n\nBe warned, it is quite filling.  Because of all the lovely [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Chilli|chilli]] flavoured [[Oil|oil]], it tempts you to eat far too much [[Bread|bread]]. This version is as close as I could get to the best we had while there.  Increase or reduce the garlic and chilli to taste. 1 bulb of garlic would be my personal choice!\n\nGood fresh [[Bread|bread]] is an essential [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] to this dish.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 300g large fresh raw [[Peeled prawns|peeled prawns]] ([[King prawns|king prawns]])\n| 125 ml [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]]\n| 3 small dried red [[chillies]], such as [[bird eye chillies]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 1 bulb of [[garlic]] broken into cloves, peeled and sliced\n}}\n'''to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| A little chopped fresh [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| 1 [[Lemon|lemon]] cut into [[Wedges|wedges]]\n| Freshly [[Baked|baked]] [[Brown bread|brown bread]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] over a medium heat, in a small pan. Not too hot, burnt [[Garlic|garlic]] is nasty.\n| Add \u00bd a teaspoon of salt to the oil and then add the [[Dried Chillies|dried chillies]] and the sliced [[Garlic|garlic]] and let them sizzle.\n| The very second you see the garlic take the slightest colour add all of the [[Prawns|prawns]]\n| Carefully stir until the [[Prawns|prawns]] turn pink\n| Be careful not to overcook the garlic.  You want it soft and juicy, not crisp and dry.\n| Pour the contents of the pan into a pre-warmed [[Oven|oven]]-proof dish, or serve from the pan on a wooden board\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nSprinkle the chopped [[Parsley|parsley]] over the [[Brown bread|brown bread]] and serve this [[Tapa|tapa]] with [[Lemon wedges|lemon wedges]]\n===Recipe source===\n\n* A glorious Menorcan holiday\n===Variations===\nMy preference for the [[chillies]] is to use 3 large dried [[Chile de Arbole]], cut into small pieces.  This way, the oil gets properly flavoured and you have lots of lovely garlic flavoured chillies to eat - I do like my chillies to have a little bite!\n==See also==\n* [[Gambas al Ajillo]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlic #brownbread #menorcangarlicprawns #parsley #bread #prawns #tapa #chillies #panfried #gambasalajillo #wedges </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Merluza a la gallega (Galician style hake)",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Merluza a la gallega (Galician style hake) a Spanish recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#hake #potatoes #garlic #onion #parsley #paprika #bayleaves #simmer #cod #bayleaf #onions \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is a very quick and easy recipe from Galicia which is known as Merluza a Galega in Galician\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1853\n|PortionCalories = 463\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Merluza a la gallega (Galician style hake) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Not a fan of hake\u2026</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">\u2026but all that garlic makes this recipe pretty tasty!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is a very quick and easy recipe from Galicia which is known as '''Merluza \u00e1 Galega''' in Galician.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 800g [[Hake]] fillets or 4 hake steaks weighing about 200-225g each\n| [[Salt]]\n| 4 large [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and thickly sliced\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], sliced\n| 1 [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]\n| 4 sprigs [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| 120ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 8 or more Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], sliced\n| 1 tablespoon sweet [[Paprika|paprika]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Season the [[Hake|hake]] with the [[Salt|salt]] .\n| Place the [[Potatoes|potatoes]],  [[Onion|onion]],  [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]] and [[Parsley|parsley]] with some [[Salt|salt]] in a saucepan and cover with water.\n| [[Boil]] for about 10 minutes.\n| Reduce the heat, add the [[Hake|hake]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for a further 10 minutes.\n| If using fillets add them a few minutes later as they do not hold together as well as steaks.\n| Towards the end of the cooking time, heat the [[Oil|oil]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] until golden.\n| Drain the [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Onion|onion]] and the [[Hake|hake]], discarding the [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]] and [[Parsley|parsley]] and plate up.\n| Remove the [[Garlic|garlic]] from the heat immediately and quickly stir in the [[Paprika|paprika]].\n| Pour the [[Garlic|garlic]] [[Sauce|sauce]] over the [[Hake|hake]], [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and [[Onions|onions]].\n}}\n===Variations===\nSee our recipe for [[Merluza a la Gallega (with chorizo)]] - not authentic though!\n[[Hake]] can be difficult to find in some parts of the UK, so I would suggest you use [[Cod|cod]] instead.\n===Chef's notes===\nAs mentioned above, be very careful with fillets or they will distintergrate as they are boneless. Steaks have [[bones]] which keep the flesh together better.\n\nI think it is best to use a non-[[Smoked paprika|smoked paprika]] for this dish.  [[Paprika#Piment\u00f3n de Murcia|Piment\u00f3n de Murcia]] is probably the best [[Spanish]] variety.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Hake]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes|Hake]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Hake]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Hake]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes|Hake]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Hake]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#hake #potatoes #garlic #onion #parsley #paprika #bayleaves #simmer #cod #bayleaf #onions </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Varoma / Reverse Blade / Speed Spoon'''.\n| After '''15 minutes''', put the Varoma containing the [[Fish|fish]] on top of the lid.\n| Remove the Varoma and pour the contents of the bowl into a serving dish and place the [[Fish|fish]] on top.  Reserve.\n| Put the [[Oil|oil]] in the bowl for the [[Garlic|garlic]] [[Sauce|sauce]] '''6 minutes / Temp. Varoma / Speed 1'''.\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] '''6 minutes / Temp. Varoma / Speed 1'''.\n| Finally, add the [[Paprika|paprika]] (once the [[Oil|oil]] has cooled slightly) and mix '''10 seconds / Speed 1''' (check that nothing remains on the screw of the blades).\n| Drizzle the [[Sauce|sauce]] over the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and the [[Fish|fish]], and serve immediately\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n* This is a translation of a recipe in '''''[[Thermomix]] TM31 - Imprescindible para tu cocina''''' which is the book supplied with [[Spanish]] TMXs.\n===Chef's notes===\nThe [[potato]] cooking time will vary according to the type used - I had King Edwards and chopped them quite small. 200 ml [[White wine|white wine]]\n| 400 ml [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 100 g [[Green peas|green peas]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Paprika]]\n| 50 ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 2 [[Onions|onions]], thinly sliced\n| 6 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves sliced\n| 2 soft [[Chorizo sausages|chorizo sausages]] (about 15cm each) thinly sliced \n| 1 large [[Green pepper|green pepper]] [[Julienned|julienned]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| sprig of [[Parsley|parsley]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat [[Oil|oil]] in a [[cazuela]] or high sided [[Saute|saute]] pan. \n| Add [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and cook gently until soft.\n| Add [[Chorizo|chorizo]], [[Green peppers|green peppers]] and [[Paprika|paprika]] and [[Fry|fry]] for 5/7 mins.\n| Stir in [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Peas|peas]], add [[Wine|wine]] and stock (this should just cover contents), season with [[Salt|salt]] & [[Pepper|pepper]].\n| Bring to [[Boil|boil]] and then [[Simmer|simmer]] uncovered for 10/15 mins until [[Potatoes|potatoes]] are just tender.\n| Season [[Hake|hake]] well on both sides, add on top of pan contents, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for a further 10 mins until hake is cooked through.\n| Garnish with [[Parsley|parsley]].\n}}\n===Variations===\n[[Cod|Cod]] or [[Haddock|haddock]] can be substituted for [[Hake|hake]].\n\nSee also [[Merluza a la gallega (Galician style hake)]] for a more authentic version.\n\nRecipe added by [[User:Martynst|Martin Street]] 19 September 2009\n===Authenticity?===\nComments have been Mallorcan Cookery\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1041\n|PortionCalories = 260\n|DatePublished=17th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 25 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Merluza con salsa de ajos y almendras (Hake in garlic and almond sauce) style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This worked well with basa too.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is a garlicky recipe for [[Hake|hake]], based on a recipe in Toby Molenaar's ''Discovering the Art of Mallorcan Cookery'' (ISBN 8427305648)\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 4 [[Hake|hake]] fillets dredged in seasoned [[Flour|flour]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], chopped\n| 1 bulb [[Garlic|garlic]], finely chopped\n| 2 [[Cloves garlic, crushed|cloves garlic, crushed]]\n| 12 [[Almonds|almonds]], peeled, chopped and lightly [[Toasted|toasted]] in a [[Dry frying|dry frying]] pan\n| 1 [[Hard-boiled bouillon]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and sear the [[Hake|hake]] fillets on both sides.\n| Remove the [[Hake|hake]] from the pan Steaks hold together better because of the [[bones]], but my lot don't like fiddling with [[bones]], so fillets were a better option.\n\nAlso use any [[Herbs|herbs]] you like, perhaps [[Tarragon|tarragon]] or [[Parsley|parsley]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Hake in garlic and almond sauce]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes|Hake in garlic and almond sauce]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Hake in garlic and almond sauce]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Hake in garlic and almond sauce]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes|Hake in garlic and almond sauce]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Hake in garlic and almond sauce]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#hake #bones #garlic #tarragon #panfried #fish #vegetables #boiledpotatoes #oliveoil #onion #salad </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Molletes antequeranos (Antequera muffins)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Molletes antequeranos (Antequera muffins) a Spanish recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#yeast #flour #breadmaker #driedyeast #baking #foodprocessor #kneadingbread #ferment #strongflour #unusualrecipes #ham \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Much larger than English muffins, molletes are much closer to them than they are to the American ones\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2206\n|PortionCalories = 367\n|DatePublished=12th April 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6 \n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 20 minutes \n |PrepTime = 2 hours \n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Molletes antequeranos (Antequera muffins) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">These make great burger buns</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Molletes antequeranos (TM).jpg|thumb|300px|right|Freshly baked molletes]]\nMuch larger than English muffins, molletes are much closer to them than they are to the American ones.  They are eaten at breakfast and throughout the day as a snack.  Similar versions of molletes are found throughout southern Spain.\n\nWhilst the serving suggestion I have given is typical, you can basically do what you want with them.\n\n\n'''1st dough (Masa madre):'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 100 g [[Strong flour|strong flour]] \n| 50 ml  warm water \n| 1 x 7 g sachet of [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]] (use easy blend [[Yeast|yeast]] if making in a [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]]) or 15 g fresh yeast \n}}\n \n'''2nd dough: '''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 500 g [[Strong flour|strong flour]] \n| 320 ml  warm water \n| 1 x 7 g sachet of [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]] (use easy blend [[Yeast|yeast]] if making in a [[Bread maker|bread maker]]) or 15 g fresh yeast \n| 50 ml [[Olive|olive]] or [[Sunflower oil|sunflower oil]]. \n| 2 teaspoons [[Salt|salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n'''To make the 1st dough: '''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[Yeast|yeast]] in the water and if using fresh or normal [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]], allow to [[Ferment|ferment]].\n| Add the water and the [[Yeast|yeast]] to the [[Flour|flour]] and form the dough into a ball.\n| Cut a cross on the top of the ball and place in a bowl of warm water.  The water should cover the dough and then cover the bowl with a piece of [[cling-film]]. \n| Once the dough has risen to the top of the bowl (about 10 minutes), use immediately. \n}}\n'''  To make the molletes:'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| From the 2nd dough ingredients, add the [[Yeast|yeast]] to the water, allowing to [[Ferment|ferment]] if necessary.\n| Add the [[Oil|oil]] and mix. Then add half the [[Flour|flour]] mixed with the [[Salt|salt]] and mix again\n| Next, add the 1st dough, together with the remaining 2nd dough [[Flour|flour]] and [[Kneading bread|knead]] for at least 10 minutes.  If using a machine, [[Kneading bread|knead]] until the dough is smooth and elastic. \n| Place the dough in a bowl, cover with a damp [[Tea|tea]]-towel and allow to rise in a [[warm place]] until it is double its size.  \n| Punch the dough well and divide into about 6 pieces.  Shape each piece into a sort of elongated ball place on a greased [[Baking|baking]] sheet until they have doubled in size.  This could take several hours or even overnight as there is no sugar to encourage the yeast to work.\n| Preheat the oven to 250 C/475 F/Gas 9 and placing a bowl of water in the bottom before switching on.\n| If you wish, you can lightly dust the molletes with [[Flour|flour]].\n| Once heated, put them into the oven and immediately reduce the temperature to 200 C/400 F/Gas 6 and [[Bake|bake]] for around 20 minutes.  \n| 5 minutes before the end of [[Baking|baking]], spray the molletes with water.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nLightly toast them and paint with [[Garlic|garlic]]-infused [[Olive oil|olive oil]] or melted [[lard]].  Add [[Grated|grated]] [[Tomato|tomato]] (minus the skin) and chopped Serrano or Ib\u00e9rico [[Ham|ham]].  Use more [[Oil|oil]] if desired.  Similarly, they can be used to make a form of the Mallorqu\u00edn [[Pa amb oli]] or the Catal\u00e1n [[Pa amb tom\u00e0quet]].  I like them with what I call 'cheats' [[Pa amb tom\u00e0quet|'cheats' Pa amb tom\u00e0quet]] or [[Tomate frito]].\n===Chef's notes===\nYou will probably need to use two baking trays with 3 molletes on each as they spread.  Also use the shallowest trays you have otherwise the undersides of the molletes may be still slightly doughy.  If you only have deepish trays, then after the normal cooking time, turn over the molletes and put them back into the oven for a few minutes.\n\nIt is impossible to make the dough entirely in a [[breadmaker]].  Loathe as I am to create washing-up, I decided to make them a second time using the [[food processor]] until both doughs were mixed.  I then transferred it to the [[breadmaker]] for the final kneading and first rising.  This saves standing over the [[food processor]] whilst it is kneading the dough.\n==See also==\n* [[Molletes antequeranos (Antequera muffins)]]\n* [[Eggs Benedict]]\n* [[Breakfast muffins]]\n* [[Philadelphia breakfast muffins]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Molletes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Molletes]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Molletes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Molletes]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#yeast #flour #breadmaker #driedyeast #baking #foodprocessor #kneadingbread #ferment #strongflour #unusualrecipes #ham </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

They are eaten at breakfast and throughout the day as a [[Snack|snack]]. Similar versions of molletes are found throughout southern [[Spain]]. Whilst the serving suggestion I have given is typical, you can basically do what you want with them.  They are named after the lovely town of Antequera in Andaluc\u00eda\n\n\n'''For the [[Mother dough|mother dough]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n| 100g strong [[Bread|bread]] [[Flour|flour]]\n| 50g water\n| 1 x 7g sachet of [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]] or 15g fresh [[Yeast|yeast]]\n}}\n'''For the main [[Dough|dough]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 320g water\n| 1 x 7g sachet of [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]] or 15 g fresh [[Yeast|yeast]]\n| 500g strong [[Bread|bread]] [[Flour|flour]]\n| 40g [[Olive|olive]] or [[Sunflower oil|sunflower oil]].\n| 2 teaspoons [[Salt|salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n\n'''For the [[Mother dough|mother dough]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Flour|flour]], water and [[Yeast|yeast]] to the bowl '''20 secs / Speed 3'''.\n| Scrape down the bowl, remove the blades and form the mixture into a ball.\n| Replace the blades, add the [[Dough|dough]] '''2:30 minutes /  [[Knead]]''' - because it is such a small quantity, the TM will not knead it properly unless you manually form it into a ball.\n| Remove from the bowl, shape into a ball and cut a cross in the top of it.\n| Have ready a bowl of warm water, place the [[Dough|dough]] into it and cover with [[Cling film|cling film]] or a see-through shower cap.\n}}\n'''For the main [[Dough|dough]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Immediately proceed to make the main [[Dough|dough]] by adding the water and the [[Yeast|yeast]] to the bowl '''2:30 minutes / 37\u00b0 / Speed 1'''.\n| Add the remaining ingredients to the bowl '''20 seconds / Speed 3'''.\n| Add the [[Mother dough|mother dough]], which should now be floating in the water, then '''2:30 minutes / Knead''' (If it isn't floating, wait until it does - it should take no more than 10 minutes).\n| Leave in the bowl until the [[Dough|dough]] has pushed up the MC from the lid.\n| Tip onto a lightly floured surface, removing the blades from the TM.\n| Weigh the [[Dough|dough]] and divide into 6 pieces - each piece should weigh about 180g.\n| Shape each piece into a sort of [[Cow|cow]] pat and place on a greased [[Baking|baking]] sheet until they have doubled in size. This could take several hours or even overnight as there is no [[Sugar|sugar]] to encourage the [[Yeast|yeast]] to work.\n| Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 250 C/475 F/Gas 9.\n| If you wish, you can lightly dust the molletes with [[Flour|flour]].\n| Once heated, put them into the [[Oven|oven]], and place a bowl on the oven floor.\n| Fill the bowl with [[Boiling|boiling]] water and immediately reduce the temperature to 200 C/400 F/Gas 6.\n| [[Bake]] for around 20 minutes.\n| 5 minutes before the end of [[Baking|baking]], you can [[Spray|spray]] the molletes with water.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nLightly toast them and paint with [[Garlic|garlic]]-infused [[Olive oil|olive oil]] or melted [[Lard|lard]]. Add [[Grated|grated]] [[Tomato|tomato]] (minus the skin) and chopped [[Serrano]] or Ib\u00e9rico [[Ham|ham]]. Use more [[Oil|oil]] if desired. \n===Recipe source===\n* Adapted for [[Thermomix]] from a recipe I found on a [[Spanish]] web site a few years ago and can no longer find.\n===Chef's notes===\nYou will probably need to use two [[Baking|baking]] trays with 3 molletes on each as they spread. Also use the shallowest trays you have otherwise the undersides of the molletes may be still slightly doughy. If you only have deepish trays, then after the normal cooking time, turn over the molletes and put them back into the [[Oven|oven]] for a few minutes. \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#dough #yeast #flour #baking #motherdough #driedyeast #bread #thermomixrecipes #lard #knead #snack </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

title": "Molletes antequeranos - Antequera muffins (V)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Molletes antequeranos - Antequera muffins a Spanish recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#yeast #breadmaker #flour #driedyeast #baking #kneadingbread #foodprocessor #ferment #strongflour #olive #grated \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Much larger than English muffins, Thermomix molletes are much closer to them than they are to the American ones\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2206\n|PortionCalories = 367\n|DatePublished=8th March 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6 \n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 20 minutes + overnight\n |PrepTime = 2 hours plus overnight rise\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Molletes antequeranos (Antequera muffins) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Julia's favourite rolls</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Though I bet she'd have crushed garlic in them!  \ud83d\ude0a</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Freshly baked molletes.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Freshly baked molletes]]\nMuch larger than English muffins, molletes are much closer to them than they are to the American ones.  They are eaten at breakfast and throughout the day as a snack.  Similar versions of molletes are found throughout southern Spain.\n\nWhilst the serving suggestion I have given is typical, you can basically do what you want with them.\n\n\n'''1st dough (Masa madre):'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 100 g [[Strong flour|strong flour]] \n| 50 ml  warm water \n| 1 x 7 g sachet of [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]] (use easy blend [[Yeast|yeast]] if making in a [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]]) or 15 g fresh yeast \n}}\n \n'''2nd dough: '''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 500 g [[Strong flour|strong flour]] \n| 320 ml  warm water \n| 1 x 7 g sachet of [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]] (use easy blend [[Yeast|yeast]] if making in a [[Bread maker|bread maker]]) or 15 g fresh yeast \n| 50 ml [[Olive|olive]] or [[Sunflower oil|sunflower oil]]. \n| 2 teaspoons [[Salt|salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n\n'''To make the 1st dough: '''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[Yeast|yeast]] in the water and if using fresh or normal [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]], allow to [[Ferment|ferment]].\n| Add the water and the [[Yeast|yeast]] to the [[Flour|flour]] and form the dough into a ball.\n| Cut a cross on the top of the ball and place in a bowl of warm water.  The water should cover the dough and then cover the bowl with a piece of [[cling-film]]. \n| Once the dough has risen to the top of the bowl (about 10 minutes), use immediately.\n}}\n'''To make the molletes:'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| From the 2nd dough ingredients, add the [[Yeast|yeast]] to the water, allowing to [[Ferment|ferment]] if necessary.\n| Add the [[Oil|oil]] and mix. Then add half the [[Flour|flour]] mixed with the [[Salt|salt]] and mix again\n| Next, add the 1st dough, together with the remaining 2nd dough [[Flour|flour]] and [[Kneading bread|knead]] for at least 10 minutes.  If using a machine, [[Kneading bread|knead]] until the dough is smooth and elastic. \n| Place the dough in a bowl, cover with a damp [[Tea|tea]]-towel and allow to rise in a [[warm place]] until it is double its size.  \n| Punch the dough well and divide into about 6 pieces.  Shape each piece into a sort of elongated ball place on a greased [[Baking|baking]] sheet until they have doubled in size.  This could take several hours or even overnight as there is no sugar to encourage the yeast to work.\n| Preheat the oven to 250 C/475 F/Gas 9 and placing a bowl of water in the bottom before switching on.\n| If you wish, you can lightly dust the molletes with [[Flour|flour]].\n| Once heated, put them into the oven and immediately reduce the temperature to 200 C/400 F/Gas 6 and [[Bake|bake]] for around 20 minutes.  \n| 5 minutes before the end of [[Baking|baking]], spray the molletes with water.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nLightly toast them and paint with [[Garlic|garlic]]-infused [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and [[Grated|grated]] [[Tomato|tomato]] (minus the skin).  Use more [[Oil|oil]] if desired.  Similarly, they can be used to make a form of the Mallorqu\u00edn [[Pa amb oli]] or the Catal\u00e1n [[Pa amb tom\u00e0quet]].  I like them with what I call 'cheats' [[Pa amb tom\u00e0quet|'cheats' Pa amb tom\u00e0quet]] or [[Tomate frito]].\n===Chef's notes===\nYou will probably need to use two baking trays with 3 molletes on each as they spread.  Also use the shallowest trays you have otherwise the undersides of the molletes may be still slightly doughy.  If you only have deepish trays, then after the normal cooking time, turn over the molletes and put them back into the oven for a few minutes.\n\nIt is impossible to make the dough entirely in a [[breadmaker]].  Loathe as I am to create washing-up, I decided to make them a second time using the [[food processor]] until both doughs were mixed.  I then transferred it to the [[breadmaker]] for the final kneading and first rising.  This saves standing over the [[food processor]] whilst it is kneading the dough.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Molletes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Molletes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Molletes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Molletes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Molletes]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes|Mol]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#yeast #breadmaker #flour #driedyeast #baking #kneadingbread #foodprocessor #ferment #strongflour #olive #grated </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Monkfish served in LOTS of garlic chilli oil",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Monkfish served in LOTS of garlic chilli oil recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#monkfish #garlic #lime #menorcangarlicprawns #chillies #blackpepper #ciabattabread #monkfishservedinlotsofgarlicchillioil #bread #chilli #driedchillies \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=1 bulb of garlic, hot chillies, half a pint of olive oil, chinks of monkfish and fresh bread to dip it in - what could be better?\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 339\n|PortionCalories = 169\n|DatePublished=25th July 2015\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour 25 minutes\n|PrepTime =  1 hour 10 minutes\n|CookTime =  15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Monkfish served in lots of garlic chilli oil.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A great meal for your special bread</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Fish \u2795 chili \u2795 garlic \u2795 good bread = \ud83d\udc96!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is a variation of [[Menorcan garlic prawns]] using [[monkfish]] instead of [[king prawns]].\n[[Image:Monkfish in garlic and chilli oil ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|This is all you need for a fantastic meal]]\n\nBe warned, it is quite filling.  Because of all the lovely [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Chilli|chilli]] flavoured [[Oil|oil]], it tempts you to eat far too much [[Bread|bread]]. Increase or reduce the garlic and chilli to taste. 1 bulb of garlic and 3 chillies is my personal choice.\n\nGood fresh [[ciabatta bread]] is an essential [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] to this dish.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 260 g skinned [[monkfish]] tail chopped into bite sized pieces (about the same size as large prawns)\n| 125 ml [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]]\n| A pinch of freshly ground [[black pepper]]\n| 3 small dried red [[chillies]], such as [[bird eye chillies]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 1 bulb of [[garlic]] broken into cloves, peeled and sliced\n| The zest and juice of 1 fresh [[lime]]\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\nThe [[monkfish]] tail has just one gelatinous bone down the centre, similar to [[rock salmon]] or [[dogfish]].  Running a sharp knife along the bone will separate the meat fairly easily.  Just check that there are no pin-[[bones]] left where the fins have been poorly trimmed.\n\nPop the [[monkfish]] chunks into a [[Lock and Lock]] box together with the juice and zest of a [[lime]].  Shake well and store in the fridge for at least an hour.\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add a pinch of [[black pepper]] and the [[olive oil]] to a small pan and heat over a medium flame. Not too hot, burnt [[Garlic|garlic]] is nasty.\n| Add \u00bd a teaspoon of salt to the oil and then add the [[Dried Chillies|dried chillies]] and the sliced [[Garlic|garlic]] and let it sizzle.\n| Drain the lime juice from the [[monkfish]] pieces and discard it. \n| The very second you see the [[garlic]] take the slightest colour, carefully add all of the [[monkfish]] pieces.\n| Cook for 3 minutes being careful not to overcook the garlic.  You want it soft and juicy, not crisp and dry.\n| Allow the oil to cool a little, then pour the contents of the pan into a pre-warmed [[Oven|oven]]-proof dish and serve from the pan on a wooden board\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nSprinkle the chopped [[thyme]] over the slices of [[ciabatta bread]] and serve this with [[Lemon wedges|lemon wedges]]\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Inspired by a glorious Menorcan holiday\n===Variations===\nMy preference for the [[chillies]] is to use 3 large dried [[Chile de Arbole]], cut into small pieces.  This way, the oil gets properly flavoured and you have lots of lovely garlic flavoured chillies to eat - I do like my chillies to have a little bite!\n==See also==\n* [[Gambas al Ajillo]]\n* [[Menorcan garlic prawns]]\n* [[Monkfish and prawns with garlic, chilli and ginger]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#monkfish #garlic #lime #menorcangarlicprawns #chillies #blackpepper #ciabattabread #monkfishservedinlotsofgarlicchillioil #bread #chilli #driedchillies </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Morcilla blanca",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Morcilla blanca, Spanish recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#morcillablanca #rice #bayleaves #stock #sausages #ham #boil #butter #ground #oregano #onion \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Literally 'white black-pudding', morcilla blanca is a Spanish sausage made without blood. For this recipe, you do not need a sausage machine or casings\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2444\n|PortionCalories = 407\n|DatePublished=9th February 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 6 large [[Sausages|sausages]]\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 2 hours\n |PrepTime = 1 hour\n |CookTime = 1 hour\n |Image = [[Image:Morcilla blanca recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice and white</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Julia, you must have put lots of time into this.  Looks really good.  Thank you!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nLiterally 'white [[black-pudding]]', [[Morcilla|morcilla]] blanca is a [[Spanish]] [[Sausage|sausage]] made without [[Blood|blood]].\n[[Image:Wrapped in butter muslin.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Wrapped in butter muslin]]\n\nFor this recipe, you do not need a [[Sausage machine|sausage machine]] or casings.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 300 ml [[Ham|ham]] [[Stock|stock]]\n| 4 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 70 g Bomba or other Valencian [[Rice|rice]]\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], finely [[Diced|diced]]\n| 1 bulb [[Garlic, crushed|garlic, crushed]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Dried|dried]] [[Oregano|oregano]]\n| 2 teaspoons sweet [[paprika|Piment\u00f3n de La Vera]]\n| 2 teaspoons hot [[paprika|Piment\u00f3n de La Vera]]\n| [[Black pepper]] as desired, [[Ground|ground]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Ground|ground]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Cloves|cloves]], [[Ground|ground]]\n| [[Nutmeg]] as desired, [[Grated|grated]]\n| 750 g [[Gloucester]] Old Spot [[Pork belly|belly pork]], [[Minced|minced]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n| 1 [[Egg|egg]], beaten\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]] (optional \u2013 this depends on the saltiness of your [[Ham|ham]] [[Stock|stock]])\n| 3 sheets of [[Butter|butter]] muslin, measuring at least 70 cm by 50 cm each\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Bring the [[Ham|ham]] [[Stock|stock]] to the [[Boil|boil]] with 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]] and the [[Rice|rice]].\n| Cover, and allow to [[Simmer|simmer]] gently until the [[Rice|rice]] has absorbed all of the [[Stock|stock]] \u2013 around 15-20 minutes.\n| Transfer to a bowl, discarding the [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]] and leave to cool.\n| Meanwhile, [[Boil|boil]] the [[Diced|diced]] [[Onions|onions]] for 5 minutes and drain them, transferring the liquid into a large saucepan with the 2 remaining [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]].\n| Add the [[Onions|onions]] to the [[Rice|rice]], together with the Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]], the [[Oregano|oregano]] and the [[Spices|spices]] and mix thoroughly with a fork.\n| Using your hands, mix in the [[Belly pork|belly pork]], [[Sherry|sherry]] and beaten [[Egg|egg]] to the [[Rice|rice]] mixture.\n| Weigh the mixture and divide into three.\n| Fold the [[Butter|butter]] muslin in half lengthways.\n| Roll out each portion into a length of about 28 cm and place on the edge of the lengthways side of muslin.\n| Roll up as tightly as you can and tie each end as tightly as possible with string.  At one end, loop an extra piece of string through to allow the [[Sausages|sausages]] to hang.\n| Tie an extra piece of string around the middle of each roll so that you get a link of two.\n| Place on a flat surface, such as a tray or [[Baking|baking]] tin and put in [[Freezer|freezer]] for 30 minutes.  This will [[Help|help]] the morcillas to bond.\n| Bring the [[Onion|onion]] water to the [[Boil|boil]] and add the morcillas.  Add extra water to cover and [[Salt|salt]] if necessary,\n| Reduce heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 30-40 minutes.\n| Remove the morcillas from the pan, drain and allow to hang in a cool larder for several hours.\n| Release them from the [[Butter|butter]] muslin and keep in the [[Fridge|fridge]] in a container for up to 4 days.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThe [[Sausages|sausages]] are best sliced and [[Fried|fried]], rather than eaten whole, in the same way that an English [[black-pudding]] would be used.\n===Variations===\nYou can vary the amount of [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Spices|spices]] and use ordinary [[Paprika|paprika]] if you wish.  If you can get it, use the [[Pork|pork]] of an Ib\u00e9rico breed of [[Pig|pig]].  The cloves are quite powerful so you may wish to reduce the quantity.\n===Chef's notes===\nYou need to be very careful when cutting the string and unrolling the morcillas.  Use very sharp, fine scissors (such as embroidery scissors) and unroll very slowly and carefully.  Keep them on a flat surface whilst doing this, or they will break. \n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Morcilla blanca]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes|Morcilla blanca]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Morcilla blanca]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Morcilla blanca]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Morcilla blanca]]\n[[Category:Starters|Morcilla blanca]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#morcillablanca #rice #bayleaves #stock #sausages #ham #boil #butter #ground #oregano #onion </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Moros y Cristianos, Spanish recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#morosycristianos #chorizo #rice #paprika #garlic #bacon #beans #spanish #oliveoil #meats #redbeans \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Literally Moors and Christians, this Spanish dish recalls the period when much of Spain was ruled by the Moors and the Spanish attempts to re-gain\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2414\n|PortionCalories = 603\n|DatePublished=19th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Alcoy, fiesta de Moros y Cristianos\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 14 hours, 45 minutes (including overnight soak)\n |PrepTime = 12 hours, 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Alcoy, fiesta de Moros y Cristianos.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Beans and bacon</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">An Alcoy speciality.</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nLiterally Moors and Christians, this [[Spanish]] dish recalls the period when much of Spain was ruled by the Moors and the Spanish attempts to re-gain their territory.  This conflict lasted more than 700 years and culminated in the capture of Granada by the 'Catholic Kings', Isabella and Fernando in 1492.\n\nMoors and Christians festivals are still celebrated each year throughout Spain, but the most famous is that in Alcoy (Alicante).\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 300 g [[Black beans|black]], [[Red beans|red]] or [[Pinto beans|pinto beans]]\n| Water\n| 280 g cooking [[Chorizo|chorizo]], whole\n| 100 g lean [[Bacon|bacon]], chopped\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 8 Cloves [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and chopped\n| [[Salt]]\n| Sweet [[Paprika|paprika]], to taste\n| 200 g white [[Rice|rice]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Soak the [[Beans|beans]] in water overnight, and the following day, drain them and place in fresh water with the [[Chorizo|chorizo]] and [[Bacon|bacon]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for two hours. \n| After about an hour, [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] in some [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and a little [[Salt|salt]] and at the last minute add the [[Paprika|paprika]].  Add to the [[Rice|rice]] and [[Meats|meats]].\n| When the [[Beans|beans]] are done, add the [[Rice|rice]] and [[Boil|boil]] gently for 20 minutes.\n| Just before serving, remove the [[Chorizo|chorizo]], slice, return to the pan and warm through.\n}}\n===Variations===\nThis traditional [[Spanish]] dish can vary in many ways depending on the region and the chef.  The [[Chorizo|chorizo]] can be substituted for [[Pork|pork]] chops, but if the [[Stew|stew]] becomes more fatty, add more [[Paprika|paprika]] and water.  You can also add other [[Meats|meats]] such as [[Morcilla|morcilla]] or [[serrano ham]]. \nThere is also a Cuban (vegetarian) version called [[Platillo Moros y Cristianos]].\n===Chef's notes===\nDo cook the [[Chorizo|chorizo]] whole and slice at the end.  This will prevent the [[Sausage|sausage]] from disintegrating, but allow it to cook thoroughly.\n--[[User:JuliaBalbilla|JuliaBalbilla]] 09:50, 2 February 2009 (UTC)\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Moros y cristianos]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Moros y cristianos]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Moros y cristianos]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Moros y cristianos]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Moros y cristianos]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes|Moros y cristianos]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Moros y cristianos]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Moros y cristianos]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#morosycristianos #chorizo #rice #paprika #garlic #bacon #beans #spanish #oliveoil #meats #redbeans </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Varoma / Speed 3&frac12;'''.\n| Afterwards, chop '''15 seconds / Speed 5''' and push down the ingredients inside the bowl.\n| Add the [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]] in thick slices, the [[Cream|cream]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]] and the reserved [[Prawn|prawn]] [[Broth|broth]] '''10 minutes / 100\u00b0 / Reverse Blade / Speed Spoon'''.\n| One minute before the end of the cooking time add the [[Prawn|prawn]] bodies.\n| Check that the [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]] are tender.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe this [[Sauce|sauce]] with any type of [[Fish|fish]].  If you like, you can add the [[Juice|juice]] of half a [[Lemon|lemon]].\n===Recipe source===\n* This is a translation of a recipe in '''''[[Thermomix]] TM31 - Imprescindible para tu cocina'''''which is the book supplied with [[Spanish]] TMXs\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#prawns #mushrooms #prawn #garlic #sauce #thermomix #spanish #butter #whitewine #leeks #broth </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Olive oil powder",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Olive oil powder recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#oliveoil #oliveoilpowder #tapiocamaltodextrin #sieve #maltodextrin #fridge #salad #moleculargastronomy #zorbit #fat #starchy \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=An easy introduction to molecular gastronomy. Powders made from oil have a magic of their own\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 370\n|PortionCalories = 61\n|DatePublished=12th September 2014\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Servings: 6 - About 150ml\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  10 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Olive oil powder recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">The Fat Duck</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">...would probably have had this on the menu!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nAn easy introduction to [[Molecular gastronomy|molecular gastronomy]], powders made from [[Oil|oil]] have a magic of their own.  You must ensure that you measure the two ingredients by '''volume''' and not by weight.  In general the [[Maltodextrin|maltodextrin]] should be twice the volume of the [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 50ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 100ml [[Tapioca maltodextrin]] (also sold as [[Zorbit]] or [[El Bull\u00ed Texturas Malto]])\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Simply mix the [[Tapioca maltodextrin]] gradually with the [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| Pass through a [[Sieve|sieve]] \n| If a more powdery texture is desired, pass through a [[Sieve|sieve]] once more, using a finer mesh\n| Store in a container in the [[Fridge|fridge]] until required\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nSprinkle over [[Salad|salad]] leaves or any [[Ingredient|ingredient]] that would normally be dressed in, or drizzled with [[Olive oil|olive oil]].  For the best effect make sure that the surface of the ingredients is as dry as possible\n===Variations===\nYou can use almost any [[Oil|oil]] you like instead of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n===Chef's notes===\nWhilst it is plainly obvious that the addition of a sufficient quantity of [[Starchy|starchy]] powder to [[Oil|oil]] would necessarily create an oil powder, the magic happens when the powder is put into the mouth.  When you do this, the powder reverts back to the flavour and texture of pure oil.  This is because [[Tapioca maltodextrin]], whilst not [[Fat|fat]] soluble, ''is'' water soluble, which is why you should only sprinkle it on ingredients which have been patted dry.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Molecular gastronomy recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#oliveoil #oliveoilpowder #tapiocamaltodextrin #sieve #maltodextrin #fridge #salad #moleculargastronomy #zorbit #fat #starchy </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Olleta de la Valle de Guadalest a Spanish recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#olletadelavalledeguadalest #rice #pork #stock #kohlrabi #garlic #bacon #beans #saffron #paprika #onions \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=An olleta is a type of very thick stew, often made with rice and is typical of the cuisine of the province of Alicante\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1874\n|PortionCalories = 468\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = The cats of Guadalest. Waiting and watching on park benches.\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Cats of Guadalest.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Ahh, bless!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Love the cats</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n \n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nAn olleta is a type of very thick [[Stew|stew]], often made with [[Rice|rice]] and is typical of the cuisine of the province of Alicante.  This particular recipe originates from the beautiful Valley of Guadalest.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 250 g [[White beans|white beans]], which have been soaked overnight\n| 400 g [[Kohlrabi|kohlrabi]] or [[Turnips|turnips]], peeled and chopped\n| 250 g [[Pork|pork]] [[Meat|meat]], eg, [[Shank|shank]], [[trotter]], [[ham hocks]] and [[pig's ear]]\n| 50 g fatty [[Bacon|bacon]]\n| 4 morcillas (preferably the [[Onion|onion]] based ones, rather than the [[Rice|rice]] based), whole\n| 200 g [[paella]] or pudding [[Rice|rice]]\n| 70 ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 4 or more Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and chopped\n| 100 g [[Onions|onions]], peeled and chopped\n| Pinch of [[Saffron|saffron]], [[Ground|ground]]\n| [[Salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| 2 [[Litres|litres]] cold water or [[Ham|ham]] [[Stock|stock]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[Beans|beans]], [[Pork|pork]] and [[Bacon|bacon]] in a saucepan and pour over the water, cooking over a gentle heat.\n| In a separate pan, [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Kohlrabi|kohlrabi]] or [[Turnips|turnips]] in the [[Oil|oil]], adding the [[Paprika|paprika]] at the last minute.\n| Pour the mixture into the saucepan containing the [[Pork|pork]] and [[Beans|beans]].\n| Cook until the [[Meat|meat]] is almost tender and add [[Salt|salt]] to taste.\n| Remove the [[Meat|meat]] from the pan, chop it into pieces, and return them to the pan with the morcillas and the [[Saffron|saffron]].\n| Cook until you are left with about 1 litre of [[Stock|stock]].\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] and cook on a medium heat for about 16-18 minutes until the [[Stock|stock]] has absorbed the rice.\n| Serve, ensuring that each person has a [[Morcilla|morcilla]].\n}}\n===Variations===\nIf the idea of [[trotters]] and [[Ears|ears]] is a bit off-putting use any cheapish cut of [[Pork|pork]] you like.\n--[[User:JuliaBalbilla|JuliaBalbilla]] 21:33, 1 February 2009 (UTC)\n===Chef's notes===\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Olleta de la valle de guadalest]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork                         "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Onion soup - A Thermomix recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cheese #chickenstock #onions #soup #onion #grill #cheddarcheese #toasted #parmesan #whitepepper #spanish \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A light and slightly sweet onion soup\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1797\n|PortionCalories = 299\n|DatePublished=31st August 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 52 minutes \n|PrepTime = 5 minutes \n|CookTime = 47 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Onion soup (TM) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Ow!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Eye-wateringly good.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nA light and slightly sweet [[Onion|onion]] [[Soup|soup]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n| 130g [[Cheddar cheese]] or any cheese suitable for melting\n| 1kg [[Onions|onions]]\n| 50g [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]]\n| 1 litre [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n| [[Salt]]\n| [[White pepper]]\n| 500g water\n| 6 slices toast\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Cheese|cheese]], cut into 4, into a very dry TM bowl '''10 seconds / Speed 4'''. (If using [[Parmesan]], use a higher speed).\n| Empty into a basin and reserve.\n| Put the [[Onions|onions]] into the TM bowl '''5 seconds / Speed 4''' (you can also slice them into fine rings).\n| Remove and reserve.\n| Put the [[Oil|oil]] in the bowl '''5 minutes / Temp. Varoma / Speed 1'''.\n| Add the reserved [[Onion|onion]] '''20 minutes / Temp. Varoma / Reverse Blade / Speed Spoon'''.\n| Next, add the [[Stock|stock]] and the [[Salt|salt]] '''20 minutes / 100\u00b0 / Reverse Blade / Speed Spoon'''.\n| Add the [[Pepper|pepper]], the 500g water and more [[Salt|salt]] if necessary '''2 minutes / 100\u00b0 / Reverse Blade / Speed Spoon'''.\n| Pour into individual bowls.\n| Place in each one a slice of [[Toasted|toasted]] [[Bread|bread]] and sprinkle the [[Cheese|cheese]] over the top.\n| Place in the [[Oven|oven]] until the [[Cheese|cheese]] has melted and serve immediately.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n* This is a translation of a recipe in '''''Thermomix TM31 - Imprescindible para tu cocina''''' which is the book supplied with [[Spanish]] TMXs.\n===Variations===\nI made this today with the following differences.  I used 2 tbsps [[Bron's Spanish vegetable stock concentrate (TM)|Bron\u0092's vegetable stock]] instead of [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] (no need to add [[Salt|salt]]).  I didn\u0092t bother gratinating it in the [[Oven|oven]] as I was only making it for myself, with the remainder going in the [[Freezer|freezer]].  What I did was to make some [[Cheese|cheese]] on toast under the [[Grill|grill]], trimmed it and just plonked it in the [[Soup|soup]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cheese #chickenstock #onions #soup #onion #grill #cheddarcheese #toasted #parmesan #whitepepper #spanish </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Paella alicantina",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Paella alicantina, Spanish recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#paellaalicantina #monkfish #rice #prawns #paellera #garlic #saffron #chicken #boiledorsimmered #fishstock #tomatoes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Paella from the province of Alicante in Comunidad Valencia\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4771\n|PortionCalories = 795\n|DatePublished=7th December 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours \n |PrepTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 45 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Paella alicantina recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Not stinking ell pie?</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Sorry.  This reminded me of a Faulty Towers episode.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Paella]] from the province of Alicante in Comunidad Valencia.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 250 ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 [[\u00f1oras|\u00f1ora]], presoaked for an hour in cold water and chopped, or ground from dried state\n| Large pinch of [[Saffron|saffron]], [[Ground|ground]]\n| 1 bulb of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and chopped\n| 250 g [[Red peppers|red peppers]], chopped\n| 1.25 kg boneless [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces, chopped\n| 300 g [[Monkfish|monkfish]] tail, chopped\n| 300 g [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and crushed\n| 300 g [[Prawns|prawns]]\n| 750 g paella [[Rice|rice]]\n| 2.5 [[Litres|litres]] (approx.) water or [[Fish stock|fish stock]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[paellera]] or a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]].\n| Add the [[\u00f1oras|\u00f1ora]], [[Saffron|saffron]], [[Peppers|peppers]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Fry|fry]] gently until the garlic is beginning to turn golden.\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces and when they are half cooked, add the [[Monkfish|monkfish]],  [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Prawns|prawns]].\n| Cook for a few minutes and add the [[Rice|rice]] and water or [[Stock|stock]]. \n| Bring the mixture to the [[Boil|boil]] and then [[Simmer|simmer]] immediately for about 20 minutes until the [[Rice|rice]] has absorbed the water.\n| Whilst the [[Rice|rice]] [[Grains|grains]] should be loose, it is desirable to allow a few of them to stick to the bottom of the pan.\n}}\n===Variations===\nI couldn't obtain [[monkfish]] on the day I required it for this recipe, so I substituted it with red snapper.  Like [[monkfish]], [[red snapper]] is not bony and its skin is a pretty colour too.  However, it is rarely used in traditional Spanish cuisine.\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you cannot find [[\u00f1oras]], [[Ancho peppers|ancho peppers]] can be substituted. \n\nHaving tried this recipe, my advice would be to buy a [[paellera]] if you are making this for 4 or more people.  I made it for 4 and it was very difficult to fit in all the ingredients in my largest, deepest frying pan.\n\nIf the tomatoes are quite juicy, reduce the amount of stock.\n--[[User:JuliaBalbilla|JuliaBalbilla]] 20:51, 1 February 2009 (UTC)\n===Paella recipes===\n* '''[[Paella alicantina]]'''\n* '''[[Vegetarian paella]]'''\n* '''Another [[Vegetarian paella (2)|Vegetarian paella]]\n* '''[[Traditional seafood paella]]'''\n* '''[[Traditional meat paella]]'''\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Paella alicantina]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes|Paella alicantina]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Paella alicantina]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Paella alicantina]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes|Paella alicantina]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes|Paella alicantina]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Paella alicantina]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#paellaalicantina #monkfish #rice #prawns #paellera #garlic #saffron #chicken #boiledorsimmered #fishstock #tomatoes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
